Controls how many pixels each \"Black boxes within the QR code\" of the QR code is. More Information see: \u003ca href=\"https://pypi.org/project/qrcode/3.0/\" rel=\"nofollow\"\u003eqrcode 3.0 Parameter \"box_size\"\u003c/a\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eExperience: The larger the value, the larger the QR code image file will be. It also takes longer to create the image file. If a value that is too small is used, the QR code may become unscaled if label_qr_width and label_qr_height have values that are too large.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cdiv class=\"highlight highlight-source-python notranslate position-relative overflow-auto\" dir=\"auto\" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content=\"'qr_box_size': 4, # DEFAULT\"\u003e\u003cpre\u003e\u003cspan class=\"pl-s\"\u003e'qr_box_size'\u003c/span\u003e: \u003cspan class=\"pl-c1\"\u003e4\u003c/span\u003e, \u003cspan class=\"pl-c\"\u003e# DEFAULT\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/pre\u003e\u003c/div\u003e\n\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003cli\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003e\u003ccode\u003eqr_border\u003c/code\u003e:\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eFor the image file: This value is used to create the QR code image file. More Information see: \u003ca href=\"https://pypi.org/project/qrcode/3.0/\" rel=\"nofollow\"\u003eqrcode 3.0 Parameter \"qr_border\"\u003c/a\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eExperience: Value 0, as the size of the QR code can be better influenced by 'label_qr_width', label_qr_height and the centered positioning creates a margin. The size of the QR code can therefore be better adjusted. performance high, the image should be as small as necessary. An image with 1920x1200px and 30MB is nonsensical if it is to be 1.00x3.00cm in size at the end. The larger the image, the longer the Base64 text. If possible, the logo is completely black and not gray or colored, which makes it even smaller. (Sufficient for thermal transfer printers).\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eHere are a few helpful online tools:\nResize image online (in mm): \u003ca is an HTML block that contains the image {{ logo }} as well as the name {{ obj.name }} and the ID of the object {{ obj.id }} in 3 lines.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cdiv class=\"highlight highlight-source-python notranslate position-relative overflow-auto\" dir=\"auto\" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content=\"'text_template': '\u0026lt;div style=\u0026quot;display: inline-block; height: class=\"pl-s\"\u003e'text_template'\u003c/span\u003e: \u003cspan class=\"pl-s\"\u003e'\u0026lt;div style=\"display: inline-block; height: 5mm; width: 15mm\"\u0026gt;\u0026lt;img src=\"{{ logo }}\" style=\"width:100%; height:100%; object-fit:fill;\"\u0026gt;\u0026lt;/div\u0026gt;\u0026lt;br\u0026gt;{{ obj.name }}\u0026lt;br\u0026gt;Device: {{ obj.id }}\u0026lt;br\u0026gt;'\u003c/span\u003e,\u003c/pre\u003e\u003c/div\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eℹ️ The image links used in the examples are merely placeholders and are not predefined by the plugin. You can therefore freely adapt them to suit your environment. Links with http:// or https:// should also work as long as the client can access them. The NetBox media link used in the example is only one possible variant that has been successfully tested in a classic NetBox installation. As a guide, the media path used in the example is usually located in the following directory: /opt/netbox/netbox/media/\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eℹ️ The logo link can be inserted directly in the text_template, but this is not recommended as the logo parameter may be included in the standard layout in future versions.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cdiv class=\"markdown-heading\"
